  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

              <div id="descriptionmodule" class="module toggle-wrap">
               <div id="descriptionmodule_heading" class="mod-header">
                <ul class="ops"></ul>
                <h2 class="toggle-title">Description</h2>
               </div>
               <div class="mod-content">
                <div id="description-val" class="field-ignore-highlight"> 
                 <div class="user-content-block"> 
                  <p>A user reported potential class loader leaks in Derby</p> 
                  <p>...The first one looks like Derby created a long-running<br> thread and copying the context class loader. To fix, the<br> context class loader should be saved/set/restored around the<br> creation of the new thread so that it copies some benign class<br> loader instead (e.g., null or getClass().getClassLoader()):</p> 
                  <p> 0x42278e58 java/lang/Thread@302e302e<br> <span class="error">[truncating at running thread LEAK]</span></p> 
                  <p>Object: 0x42278e58 java/lang/Thread@302e302e<br> Children:<br> 0x42278ee0 java/lang/String@303f303f<br> 0x4226e558 java/lang/ThreadGroup@6f2e6f2e<br> 0x42278e40<br> org/apache/derby/impl/services/monitor/AntiGC@603a603a<br> 0x419cfac0</p> 
                  <p>The second is another long running thread. The same applies:</p> 
                  <p> 0x426fe7a0 java/lang/Thread@19901990<br> <span class="error">[truncating at running thread LEAK]</span></p> 
                  <p>Object: 0x426fe7a0 java/lang/Thread@19901990<br> Parents:<br> 0x4226e5a8 [Ljava/lang/Thread;@6f386f38<br> 0x426fe548<br> org/apache/derby/iapi/services/context/ContextManager@19421942<br> Children:<br> 0x426fe838 java/lang/String@19a319a3<br> 0x4226e558 java/lang/ThreadGroup@6f2e6f2e<br> 0x426fe4f8<br> org/apache/derby/impl/services/daemon/BasicDaemon@19381938<br> 0x419cfac0</p> 
                  <p>The third is a TimerThread owneed , which is created when a<br> Timer is created. The same applies:</p> 
                  <p> 0x425ac538 java/util/Timer$TimerImpl@6b8a6b8a<br> <span class="error">[truncating at running thread LEAK]</span></p> 
                  <p>Object: 0x425ac538 java/util/Timer$TimerImpl@6b8a6b8a<br> Parents:<br> 0x41faaf58 [Ljava/lang/Thread;@3c583c58</p> 
                  <p>Object: 0x425ac510 java/util/Timer@6b856b85<br> Parents:<br> 0x425ac500<br> org/apache/derby/impl/services/timer/SingletonTimerFactory@56e25<br> 6e2</p> 
                  <p>For more info, see thread at:<br> <a href="http://www.nabble.com/ClassLoader-leaks--td18121374.html" class="external-link" rel="nofollow">http://www.nabble.com/ClassLoader-leaks--td18121374.html</a></p> 
                 </div> 
                </div> 
               </div>
              </div>

\u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eI don\'t know enough about class loading issues to tell whether or not the approach is OK. If not, I would think it was the application\'s responsibility to unload the driver when it wants all resources to be freed. \\n \\n\\n\\n Other than that, the patch looks fine to me. Wanvik  in branch \'code\\/trunk\' \\n[  https:\\/\\/svn.apache.org\\/r1620379  ] \\n\\n   DERBY-6619   After silently swallowing SecurityExceptions, Derby can leak class loaders \\n\\n Patch derby-6619-2. \\n\\n The fix introduced in   DERBY-3745   correctly is there in order to \\nprotect against the case where the thread that starts Derby, has a \\ncontext class loader that is different from the system class \\nloader. In such cases, if the timer thread inherits the context class \\nloader, the context class loader will stay in memory until the Derby \\nengine is shut down, even if all other references to the class loader \\nare gone. \\n\\n If the context class loader is the same as the system class loader, on \\nthe other hand, such a \\\"leak\\\" would not be a problem, since the system \\nclass loader will stay in memory until the JVM is shut down anyway. \\n\\n We take advantage of this and only attempt to change the context class \\nloader if it is different from the system class loader.  With this \\npatch, no warning is printed to derby.log when starting the server \\nfrom the command line, and there\'s no warning when starting the server \\nusing the API with a security manager installed when the context class \\nloader hasn\'t been changed from the default. However, if the server is \\nstarted using the API with a non-default context class loader, we do \\nsee warnings in derby.log if a security manager is installed and the \\npermission to set the class loader is missing. \\n\\n Added tests for this behavior. Moved utility methods from \\nUpgradeClassLoader to ClassLoaderTestSetup, a new decorator. It seemed \\nmore logical to put them there to allow reuse.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-14109356\\\" class=\\\"issue-data-block activity-comment twixi-block  expanded\\\"\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap verbose actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Collapse comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-expanded\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eHide\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-links\\\"\u003e\\n                \u003ca href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/DERBY-3745?focusedCommentId=14109356&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-14109356\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click and copy link for a permanent link to this comment.\\\" class=\\\"activitymodule-link issue-comment-action\\\"\u003e\\n                    \u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-link\\\"\u003ePermalink\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n                                            \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details\\\"\u003e        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"jira-bot\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_14109356_verbose\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=jira-bot\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"jira-bot\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e ASF subversion and git services\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - Wanvik  in branch \'code\\/trunk\' \\n[  https:\\/\\/svn.apache.org\\/r1620385  ] \\n\\n   DERBY-6619   After silently swallowing SecurityExceptions, Derby can leak class loaders \\n\\n Patch derby-6619-2-refinement which implements the following \\nrefinements to the test to avoid changing the context class loader in \\nSingletonTimerFactory (suggested by Knut): \\n\\n The orginal test tested against the system class loader. This new patch will: \\n\\n 1) Check if the context class loader is the same as the loader of the \\nSingletonTimerFactory class (that is, the class loader from which \\nDerby classes are loaded). Even if this isn\'t the same as the system \\nclass loader, it would be safe to skip the workaround for   DERBY-3745  , \\nsince the class loader for the Derby classes would not be eligible for \\ngarbage collection until the engine is shut down anyway. This would \\nprevent some more false positives from being reported in \\nderby.log. I\'d assume this is a kind of false positive that could \\neasily occur in an application server environment where the Derby \\nclasses are not found on the system class loader. \\n\\n 2) Check against Thread.class.getClassLoader() instead of \\nClassLoader.getSystemClassLoader(). Normally, those two checks would \\nbe identical. If however the setup is such that they aren\'t identical, \\nwe\'d still know that the class loader actually used for system classes \\nsuch as the Thread class would have to stay in memory for as long as \\nthe timer thread is alive, regardless of the context class loader of \\nthe thread, so the workaround for   DERBY-3745   can be skipped if it\'s \\nthe same as the context class loader. In such cases, if the timer thread inherits the context class\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nloader, the context class loader will stay in memory until the Derby\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nengine is shut down, even if all other references to the class loader\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nare gone.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIf the context class loader is the same as the system class loader, on\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nthe other hand, such a \\\"leak\\\" would not be a problem, since the system\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nclass loader will stay in memory until the JVM is shut down anyway.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nWe take advantage of this and only attempt to change the context class\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nloader if it is different from the system class loader. With this\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\npatch, no warning is printed to derby.log when starting the server\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nfrom the command line, and there\'s no warning when starting the server\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nusing the API with a security manager installed when the context class\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nloader hasn\'t been changed from the default. However, if the server is\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nstarted using the API with a non-default context class loader, we do\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nsee warnings in derby.log if a security manager is installed and the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\npermission to set the class loader is missing.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAdded tests for this behavior. Wanvik  in branch \'code\\/branches\\/10.11\' \\n[  https:\\/\\/svn.apache.org\\/r1620391  ] \\n\\n   DERBY-6619   After silently swallowing SecurityExceptions, Derby can leak class loaders \\n\\n Backport from trunk svn 1620378. \\n\\n Patch derby-6619-2. \\n\\n The fix introduced in   DERBY-3745   correctly is there in order to \\nprotect against the case where the thread that starts Derby, has a \\ncontext class loader that is different from the system class \\nloader. In such cases, if the timer thread inherits the context class \\nloader, the context class loader will stay in memory until the Derby \\nengine is shut down, even if all other references to the class loader \\nare gone. \\n\\n If the context class loader is the same as the system class loader, on \\nthe other hand, such a \\\"leak\\\" would not be a problem, since the system \\nclass loader will stay in memory until the JVM is shut down anyway. \\nWe take advantage of this and only attempt to change the context class \\nloader if it is different from the system class loader. With this \\npatch, no warning is printed to derby.log when starting the server \\nfrom the command line, and there\'s no warning when starting the server \\nusing the API with a security manager installed when the context class \\nloader hasn\'t been changed from the default. However, if the server is \\nstarted using the API with a non-default context class loader, we do \\nsee warnings in derby.log if a security manager is installed and the \\npermission to set the class loader is missing. \\n\\n Added tests for this behavior. Moved utility methods from \\nUpgradeClassLoader to ClassLoaderTestSetup, a new decorator. It seemed \\nmore logical to put them there to allow reuse.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-14109400\\\" class=\\\"issue-data-block activity-comment twixi-block  expanded\\\"\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap verbose actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Collapse comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-expanded\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eHide\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-links\\\"\u003e\\n                \u003ca href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/DERBY-3745?focusedCommentId=14109400&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-14109400\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click and copy link for a permanent link to this comment.\\\" class=\\\"activitymodule-link issue-comment-action\\\"\u003e\\n                    \u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-link\\\"\u003ePermalink\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n                                            \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details\\\"\u003e        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"jira-bot\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_14109400_verbose\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=jira-bot\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"jira-bot\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e ASF subversion and git services\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - This would\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nprevent some more false positives from being reported in\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nderby.log. I\'d assume this is a kind of false positive that could\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\neasily occur in an application server environment where the Derby\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nclasses are not found on the system class loader.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e2) Check against Thread.class.getClassLoader() instead of\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nClassLoader.getSystemClassLoader(). Normally, those two checks would\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nbe identical. Wanvik  in branch \'code\\/branches\\/10.11\' \\n[  https:\\/\\/svn.apache.org\\/r1620392  ] \\n\\n   DERBY-6619   After silently swallowing SecurityExceptions, Derby can leak class loaders \\n\\n Backported from trunk svn 1620385. \\n\\n Patch derby-6619-2-refinement which implements the following \\nrefinements to the test to avoid changing the context class loader in \\nSingletonTimerFactory (suggested by Knut): \\n\\n The orginal test tested against the system class loader. This new \\npatch will: \\n\\n 1) Check if the context class loader is the same as the loader of the \\nSingletonTimerFactory class (that is, the class loader from which \\nDerby classes are loaded). Even if this isn\'t the same as the system \\nclass loader, it would be safe to skip the workaround for   DERBY-3745  , \\nsince the class loader for the Derby classes would not be eligible for \\ngarbage collection until the engine is shut down anyway. This would \\nprevent some more false positives from being reported in \\nderby.log. I\'d assume this is a kind of false positive that could \\neasily occur in an application server environment where the Derby \\nclasses are not found on the system class loader. \\n\\n 2) Check against Thread.class.getClassLoader() instead of \\nClassLoader.getSystemClassLoader(). Normally, those two checks would \\nbe identical. If however the setup is such that they aren\'t identical, \\nwe\'d still know that the class loader actually used for system classes \\nsuch as the Thread class would have to stay in memory for as long as \\nthe timer thread is alive, regardless of the context class loader of \\nthe thread, so the workaround for   DERBY-3745   can be skipped if it\'s \\nthe same as the context class loader. The check will be a bit more \\nspecific this way.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\"";
